  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f5334be9-5765-45e0-a74f-4c40b74f971d'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672931526" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14019719070297193832">Pied Piper, Nevil Shute<br/><br/>Pied Piper is a novel by Nevil Shute, first published in 1942. The title is a reference to the traditional German folk tale, "The Pied Piper of Hamelin". <br/><br/>The story concerns an elderly Englishman, John Sidney Howard, who goes on a fishing holiday in France after the outbreak of the Second World War, but before the fall of France. Entrusted with the care of two English children, and overtaken by events, he attempts to return to England and safety. <br/><br/>His journey is hampered by </span>
  <span id="freeText14019719070297193832" style="display:none">Pied Piper, Nevil Shute<br /><br />Pied Piper is a novel by Nevil Shute, first published in 1942. The title is a reference to the traditional German folk tale, "The Pied Piper of Hamelin". <br /><br />The story concerns an elderly Englishman, John Sidney Howard, who goes on a fishing holiday in France after the outbreak of the Second World War, but before the fall of France. Entrusted with the care of two English children, and overtaken by events, he attempts to return to England and safety. <br /><br />His journey is hampered by the unexpected speed of the Nazi invasion of France, and by the fact that he eventually finds himself entrusted with the custody of seven young children. Eventually, he and the children are stranded in Nazi-occupied France. <br /><br />As an Englishman, he is an enemy to the occupying forces. While waiting to escape France on a fishing boat, he and his charges are discovered by the Germans. Howard is accused of spying and threatened with death. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: بیست و پنجم سپتامبر سال 2003 میلادی<br /><br />نی‌نواز هاملن یا فلوت‌زن رنگارنگ هاملن (در آلمانی: به معنی موش‌گیر هامِلْن، در انگلیسی: به معنی نی‌نواز رنگین‌پوش هاملن)؛ از داستان‌های اروپایی سده‌ های میانه مربوط به شهر هاملن در آلمان است؛ موضوع این داستان رفتن یا مرگ بیشتر کودکان این شهر است و نسخه ‌های قدیمی این داستان، یک نی‌نواز سحرآمیز را علت ترک شهر توسط کودکان نامیده ‌است؛ در سده شانزده میلادی این داستان تبدیل به قصه‌ ای کامل شد به این مضمون که موش‌های مزاحم، شهر هاملن را در بر گرفته ‌بودند و روزی سر و کله نی‌نوازی رنگین ‌پوش با یک نی سحرآمیز در این شهر پیدا می‌شود و قول می‌دهد که مشکل موش در این شهر را حل کند؛ او با نواختن نی خود موفق می‌شود همه موش‌ها را از شهر به بیرون بکشاند؛ پس از آن، مردم شهر از پرداخت دستمزد توافق ‌شده به نی‌نواز خودداری می‌کنند، و او برای تلافی آن کار، با نواختن آوازی دیگر با نی خود، همه کودکان شهر را افسون کرده و به بیرون از شهر می‌کشاند و با خود می‌برد. روایت‌هایی از این داستان در میان نوشته ‌های نویسندگان گوناگون از جمله یوهان گوته، برادران گریم و رابرت براونینگ دیده می‌شود؛ گفته می‌شود اصطلاح «پی د پایپر (دادن پول نی‌نواز)» در زبان انگلیسی؛ به معنی «هر که خربزه می‌خورد پای لرزش هم می‌نشیند» است، از این داستان الهام گرفته ‌است<br />ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2633250029544557128">I have felt like a kid in a candy store lately, my books have been that good. Here’s another one that is virtually unread these days, but such a charming story and so well written. One of my favorite writers is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/21477.Nevil_Shute' title='Nevil Shute' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nevil Shute</a>. He has a style that is easy to read and so absorbing, and absorbed is exactly what I was from the moment I opened the book and found two Londoners sipping Marsala in their “club” during a bombing raid. Of the two, one is an older man who has a tale to tell and he proceeds to </span>
  <span id="freeText2633250029544557128" style="display:none">I have felt like a kid in a candy store lately, my books have been that good. Here’s another one that is virtually unread these days, but such a charming story and so well written. One of my favorite writers is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/21477.Nevil_Shute" title="Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevil Shute</a>. He has a style that is easy to read and so absorbing, and absorbed is exactly what I was from the moment I opened the book and found two Londoners sipping Marsala in their “club” during a bombing raid. Of the two, one is an older man who has a tale to tell and he proceeds to do so with such charm that even the details of his fishing expedition sing.<br /><br />In the weeks before France fell to the Germans, Mr. Howard decides to take a trip to the Jura to fish and try to forget a blow he has received. While there, he meets a couple with two children, and when the invasion begins and he realizes he must get back to England pronto, the couple ask him to take their children along. He reluctantly agrees and sets out with babes in tow on what should be a quick escape. Of course, the invasion is worse than expected and the time is past for easy escapes, so Howard and the children are in for an adventure they would rather not have. Along the course of this adventure, Howard picks up other children, increasing the risks and slowing the progress.<br /><br />I felt as if I were there. I loved the calm and sweet Mr. Howard. I thought how unlike today’s children these tykes were but also how alike all children are. I felt the weight of the responsibility and the level of patience needed from a man who has already been told he is too old to be of any help in this war. Howard puts his own life at risk to save this group of children he doesn’t know and I thought of all the real lives that were saved by such men and women and of all the lives sacrificed in such attempts. I adored the story.<br /><br />I have a dozen Nevil Shute books yet to read. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107301.A_Town_Like_Alice" title="A Town Like Alice by Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener">A Town Like Alice</a> is on my all time favorites list and I am looking forward to reading the others, one marvelous adventure at a time.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2633250029544557128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2887853" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2887853" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/180908-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184048097p2/180908.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2887853?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/180908-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781842322789" href="/book/show/647957.Pied_Piper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/180908-tatiana?shelf=contemporaryfiction">contemporaryfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2887853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17864210471083496274">Ah, this is one of my favorite books of all! Shute is a wonderful writer. His characters are quite ordinary and believable yet they are also extraordinary and wonderfully good. He gives me faith in humanity, in the world, and in the power of just calmly going about doing what needs to be done. Most people really are like this! <br/><br/>The narrative builds from a calm center and grows more and more compelling and urgent. His protagonist, a 70 year old British gentleman, goes fishing in the Jura in France</span>
  <span id="freeText17864210471083496274" style="display:none">Ah, this is one of my favorite books of all! Shute is a wonderful writer. His characters are quite ordinary and believable yet they are also extraordinary and wonderfully good. He gives me faith in humanity, in the world, and in the power of just calmly going about doing what needs to be done. Most people really are like this! <br /><br />The narrative builds from a calm center and grows more and more compelling and urgent. His protagonist, a 70 year old British gentleman, goes fishing in the Jura in France in the spring early in WW2, and gets caught up in the overrun of France by the Germans. His trip home is delayed by the needs of a couple of English children his friends at the French hotel ask him to take back to England with him. He's so patient and good with the kids as things get more and more desperate on their trip and they're finally overtaken by the advancing German army. Along the way he has picked up more kids: Rose from the hotel, Pierre whose parents were killed on the road by a German bomb, Wilhelm who's being persecuted and stoned by French villagers because he speaks Dutch they've mistaken for German. People help them along the way and he's taken in by a French family he barely knows only to find out they are more connected than he realized. This really is the most heartbreaking and beautiful story!<br /><br />Shute appeals to my geeky heart by getting every detail of the boats, planes, tanks, every physical detail, just exactly right. You can count 100% on whatever he says, in his wonderful aviation-engineer's way. This gives his tales a solidity, a truth about them, that is palpable. I love that so much about his stories. Whenever I read a book and they get some small fact wrong, some physical detail that I know isn't right, it just kills the whole thing for me and razes my carefully-suspended edifice of disbelief. Not only will Shute never do this to you, but you can learn a great deal that's interesting about sailing, flying, etc. from reading him.<br /><br />I've read this book five or six times now and it gets better every time. I really hope Nevil Shute, who was well-beloved a generation ago in Britain and Australia, I really hope he gets the attention now in the US and the rest of the world that he deserves. Just one of the best storytellers ever!<br /><br />If you want to check him out, try these titles: this one, "Pied Piper", "Round the Bend", "Trustee from the Toolroom", "No Highway", and "The Legacy" which was sold in the US under the title "A Town Like Alice". If you've read "On the Beach", the nuclear-holocaust one, realize that it's very uncharacteristic of him in a number of ways, and these others will be different in a vastly-better sort of way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17864210471083496274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1425119109" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1425119109" />
    <a title="Chrissie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/632247-chrissie"><img alt="Chrissie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321799585p2/632247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1425119109?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chrissie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chrissie" href="/user/show/632247-chrissie">Chrissie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=hf">hf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1425119109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11820963216867505627"><br/>Each author has their own special style. How would I describe Nevil Shute's? His books have a “feel good” tone, and yet at the same time they don't shy away from difficult themes. As with fairy tales, you get scary and suspenseful tidbits, but at the conclusion you feel satisfied. Content. <br/><br/>This novel is said to be based on a true life story. Yet nobody calls it non-fiction. There are just too many coincidences for me to accept this as being totally true to life. The story is about a seventy year</span>
  <span id="freeText11820963216867505627" style="display:none"><br />Each author has their own special style. How would I describe Nevil Shute's? His books have a “feel good” tone, and yet at the same time they don't shy away from difficult themes. As with fairy tales, you get scary and suspenseful tidbits, but at the conclusion you feel satisfied. Content. <br /><br />This novel is said to be based on a true life story. Yet nobody calls it non-fiction. There are just too many coincidences for me to accept this as being totally true to life. The story is about a seventy year old English man from Essex who decides to take a vacation trip to France to go fishing. He is a widower and recently his son has died. His son was RAF pilot. He misses him terribly. It is the summer of 1940, and anyone with a little knowledge of history knows that this was not the summer to traipse off to France. When things start heating up, Howard, that is the central protagonist, ends up agreeing to take two children and then another and another.... back to England. Well, finally it gets to be a total of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[seven <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>! Children of different nationalities - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[two English siblings with parents living in Switzerland, two French children of which one has an English father and the other is now an orphan, his parents killed on the road by German bombing, a very young Dutch child stoned by French villagers claiming him to be a “German spy”, a son of a Polish Jew, and one more child….which I am not going to mention even here in the spoiler because there is a final twist at the book’s end. Let's try with a spoiler within a spoiler - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The last child is the niece of a German Gestapo official.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> So with a hidden spoiler within a spoiler you see the story has a final exciting twist! This all <b>could</b> have happened. Maybe it did happen. The story is said to be true, but exactly how much of it? That is the question! <br /><br />Several aspects of the writing make the story feel genuine. The children behave as children do, and at the same time each is an individual different from the other. Each is a character with distinguishable weaknesses and strengths. And Howard, the seventy year-old, he can manage only so much! You should see what a wreck they are when they reach the end of the trip! What also makes the story feel true is that there are both villains and kind souls. The history related is accurate. <br /><br />Yet some events go too far:<br />1. Would parents <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[send their two young children, one eight and the other five, off with an elderly man whom they scarcely know <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>? It <b>is</b> possible but rather unlikely. It is more likely that the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[wife would have followed along with Howard, taking the children back to England together  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br />2. Not all Germans behaved badly during the war. They were instructed to set a good example, to show the excellence of German ways. I can understand that the child in the story is returned de-loused and clean, but that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[brand-new clothes were bought for him <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is stretching believability! <br />3. It is just too coincidental that the German Gestapo <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ also had a niece whom he wanted taken out of harm’s way. Nice that Howard was so wealthy and had a daughter willing to take care of all seven children <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>! <br /><br />I am fine with an elderly man helping kids get away from France and the war, but the coincidences are a bit thick. We have here a “feel good” story with accurate historical events and of course it <b>could</b> be possible. I would say there is a core of truth with some extra embellishments added. <br /><br />It is nice how a love story is woven in. It is satisfying that Howard <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[gets to know and hear of how his son fell in love <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Again, nothing is to say this couldn't have happened, and it is beautifully told. The horrors of war and the beauty of love are intertwined, just as it should be in both a good fairy tale and in real life.<br /><br />I enjoyed the narration of the audiobook. David Rintoul <b>can</b> and <b>does</b> speak French properly. This adds authenticity. His ability to capture how English often incorrectly pronounce French adds humor too! Very well done and easy to follow. Only a little knowledge of French is necessary to understand the untranslated lines.<br /><br />The book is satisfying and tells accurate history. I found only one silly mistake - St. Malo is in Brittany not Normandy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11820963216867505627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2967061-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577653837p2/2967061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967061-anne?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161648858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13888252916263286419">4 stars. Read Oct. 2020.<br/><br/>Another superb Nevil Shute novel. Just as good on the second read. <br/><br/>It is 1940 in England. John Howard, a 70 years old man, recently heard of the death of his son, an RAF pilot. Grieving, he decides that a vacation in a favorite spot will do him some good and he plans a trip for the Jura region of France in the spring to coincide with the blooming of the wildflowers . I wanted to be there with him, and in a way I was, through Shute's beautiful descriptions. <br/><br/>John has a love</span>
  <span id="freeText13888252916263286419" style="display:none">4 stars. Read Oct. 2020.<br /><br />Another superb Nevil Shute novel. Just as good on the second read. <br /><br />It is 1940 in England. John Howard, a 70 years old man, recently heard of the death of his son, an RAF pilot. Grieving, he decides that a vacation in a favorite spot will do him some good and he plans a trip for the Jura region of France in the spring to coincide with the blooming of the wildflowers . I wanted to be there with him, and in a way I was, through Shute's beautiful descriptions. <br /><br />John has a lovely vacation, relaxing, fishing, meeting locals and travelers alike. The war is far away at the start of his vacation but as it gets closer to France the vacationers discuss the matter. No one believes that the Germans will get very far. But as German victories mount John and the other vacationers decide it might be best to head home. One couple thinks that their 2 children would be safer in England far away from the way so they ask John if he would mind escorting their 2 children to London where they have relatives with whom they can stay. John, such a kind man who has been playing with the children during his vacation and whittling whistles for them and himself, says yes. (The whistles were a very clever way for Shute to get the musical instrument into his story of the "Pied Piper." ) The rest of the original classic plays out as John makes his way through what becomes occupied France. Given the title it isn't a spoiler to say that I was curious to see how he would add more children to his trek. He did so with twists and turns which were imaginative, sad and harrowing. The kindness, patience and resourcefulness of this sweet man never wavered throughout the obstacles blocking and delaying his journey home. Some of the obstacles were doozies and had me worried at times <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[but I kept reminding myself that Nevil Shute novels always end well.. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /> One aspect at the end of the novel strained credulity a bit but I can live with that. It's on par with Shute's positive outlook. You'll have to read the book to figure out what I mean. No spoilers here.<br /><br />A very heart-warming yet gripping story. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13888252916263286419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1425911905" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1425911905" />
    <a title="Jaksen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7233842-jaksen"><img alt="Jaksen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455934399p2/7233842.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1425911905?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaksen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaksen" href="/user/show/7233842-jaksen">Jaksen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780307474018" href="/book/show/7757032-pied-piper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7233842-jaksen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1425911905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1813468332144651563">A wonderful book! Absolutely outstanding!<br/><br/>My copy came from the library at the Mass Maritime Academy in Bourne, MA (where I also have a summer home.) I tried to get it via my home library, this was the closest copy they could find. It is part of the Complete Works of Nevil Shute, which I had no idea existed. Anyhow, I am a huge fan of Shute's novel, 'On the Beach,' and that prompted me to look for some of his other novels. <br/><br/>To the book. What a story. Supposedly based on a true story, it was told t</span>
  <span id="freeText1813468332144651563" style="display:none">A wonderful book! Absolutely outstanding!<br /><br />My copy came from the library at the Mass Maritime Academy in Bourne, MA (where I also have a summer home.) I tried to get it via my home library, this was the closest copy they could find. It is part of the Complete Works of Nevil Shute, which I had no idea existed. Anyhow, I am a huge fan of Shute's novel, 'On the Beach,' and that prompted me to look for some of his other novels. <br /><br />To the book. What a story. Supposedly based on a true story, it was told to Shute during a bombing raid in London. He's in his club, drinking, smoking, etc., when a raid begins - the year, 1942. Instead of taking refuge in the basement with the other members, Shute remains 'upstairs,' enjoying his coffee and brandy. (Well, he remains alert to what's going on and IS ready to take refuge if need be.) At any rate he runs into a man named Howard, also staying upstairs in the club and to pass the time Howard tells Shute the story of how he crossed France with several small children just as the Germans were invading. Hence the 'Pied Piper' of the novel's title. Except 70-year old Howard is a very loving, caring, concerned and provident piper, unlike the one of legend. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Finishing up a vacation in France, Howard agrees to escort two English children home because it's not safe in Geneva, which is where they live. Seriously, the talk was that Switzerland was soon to be invaded by Germany, not France. (Hindsight always is twenty-twenty.) So off Howard goes with his two young charges. They go by train, enjoying all the comforts Howard assumes are his - comfortable accommodations, excellent French food, reliable transportation, and anything his (ample) funds can afford. The first two children are only a minor inconvenience, at first. <br /><br />But along the way he picks up several more, all under different circumstances. The children are English and French, Dutch and Polish. But why was Mr. Howard in France in the first place? To go fishing, of course, the belief being that the 'trouble' in the north would never reach the south, that the French wouldn't surrender, of course not, and that Paris would 'never' be taken, and even if so, there'd be plenty of time to get out of the country. To say Mr. Howard is stupid or oblivious is far from the mark. He's a man in mourning, having recently lost his son, an RAF pilot; he knows the dangers. But apparently at this time there were many who believed this skirmish with Hitler, this small war, would be cleaned up quickly by the French, the English, and so on. (America hadn't yet entered the war.) Of course anyone who thinks this way was absolutely wrong and things deteriorate rapidly. The loss of convenient transportation, or the certainty of a place to sleep and food to eat are first to go. Howard picks up another child at the request of one of his hosts, then another who has lost his parents in a bombing raid, and then another, another, another...<br /><br />At the very end, just as it seems the French Resistance (or similar counterparts) will help Howard and all the children escape from France, the Germans are introduced, like a black cloud, complete with lightning and thunderclaps. <br /><br />If this were purely fiction a reader might feel there are two major coincidences in the storyline that don't ring true. But this was based on what Shute learned from the real man. And considering the circumstances, they aren't unbelievable. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I loved Mr. Howard, though I found some of the children hard to like, and in general I do like children. (A lot more than I like a lot of adults, btw.) But the children are portrayed very realistically, sometimes being a total delight and at others a bunch of whiny, bratty pains in the you-know-where. And still Howard fords on, gathers them up, keeps going when he's tired or feeling sick. He finds ways to distract the children, entertain them, keep them warm, fed and safe.<br /><br />This book was made into a movie in 1942, but it needs an update. I can see one of our fine 'senior' actors, either American or English, in the lead role. I'm looking for a copy of the 1942 version to watch, but I'd love to see a newer one, too.<br /><br />It's simply an all-around, well-written, great tale. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1813468332144651563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2568021581623277441">Probably a 4.5. Another typically good effort from Nevil Shute. He loves to bring us the stories of common people that are placed in uncommon or dangerous circumstances and it is very natural and easy to root for that person. Here we have an elderly British gentleman who decides to go to the French/Swiss border to fish just prior to the outbreak of WW2. While there the war breaks out and he tries to return to England. He is placed on charge of 2 children, which eventually goes to 3, then 4 & 5, </span>
  <span id="freeText2568021581623277441" style="display:none">Probably a 4.5. Another typically good effort from Nevil Shute. He loves to bring us the stories of common people that are placed in uncommon or dangerous circumstances and it is very natural and easy to root for that person. Here we have an elderly British gentleman who decides to go to the French/Swiss border to fish just prior to the outbreak of WW2. While there the war breaks out and he tries to return to England. He is placed on charge of 2 children, which eventually goes to 3, then 4 &amp; 5, etc. and this is his story of his attempt to leave France with these small children.<br />I did think that the first half of the book dragged a bit, but the last 150 pages really moved along and was a real page-turner! The book is only 304 pages in length and is a book that I read in a little over 2 days. If you are a fan of Shute you will love this book.<br />Neil Shute has taken his place on my list of favorite authors along with Steinbeck &amp; Michener. Great storytellers!!</span>

<div id="review_2850404250" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2850404250" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5837456-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372225128p2/5837456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2850404250?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/29956583-pied-piper">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2850404250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9079859034222003867">I haven’t read anything by Nevil Shute before, so I was interested to try this. However, having finished it, I feel as though this is the literary equivalent of a black and white, Sunday afternoon film. We begin in a club where the frail, elderly, John Sidney Howard (who is seventy – doesn’t seem that far off!) sits, calmly, through an air raid at his club. Shunning the shelter, he drinks by the fire, where he is joined by another man and proceeds to tell him the story of his recent trip to Euro</span>
  <span id="freeText9079859034222003867" style="display:none">I haven’t read anything by Nevil Shute before, so I was interested to try this. However, having finished it, I feel as though this is the literary equivalent of a black and white, Sunday afternoon film. We begin in a club where the frail, elderly, John Sidney Howard (who is seventy – doesn’t seem that far off!) sits, calmly, through an air raid at his club. Shunning the shelter, he drinks by the fire, where he is joined by another man and proceeds to tell him the story of his recent trip to Europe.<br /><br />After Mr Howard’s son was killed, he seemed to feel the need to travel – to France, in wartime. Well, this is hindsight, but, I would have thought that, in any war, it would be best to stay where you were. However, while in France, the situation suddenly worsens and he decides to return home. Then a couple living in Switzerland, decide, rather blithely, to ask him to take their children back to England as they want to stay together – not knowing how long the war would last. There are, it has to be said, some pretty poor decisions made in this book.<br /><br />Our elderly gent, now encumbered with both his fishing gear and the rather irritating Ronald and Shirley, head off in the train. Of course, all goes wrong, and, along the way, he ends up collecting a host of other children. A young French girl, whose father is in London, a French boy whose parents are killed, a young Dutch boy, a Jewish boy whose father has been taken away and a half-Jewish, German girl. He also discovers things about his son that he did not know, and also finds his own strength.<br /><br />Ultimately, I didn’t find this the heart-warming read I expected. It just seemed too obvious and the characters too stereotypical. The chirpy British soldiers who happily allowed a group of assorted children and an old man onto their lorry, the love story that Mr Howard unearths and the way he discovers a meaning to life, while he has a job to do. However, the ending left me feeling somewhat deflated and, ultimately, the journey just went on too long. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9079859034222003867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17837228032005868769">Pied Piper. He's among my six Shute favorites. One of those old quiet stories that stays with me. Shute has the faculty for seizing upon contemporary drama and weaving it into a story with very human elements.   <span id="freeText17837228032005868769" style="display:none">Pied Piper. He's among my six Shute favorites. One of those old quiet stories that stays with me. A gentle man's tale of WWII. <br /><br />Here's a professional review from KIRKUS REVIEW<br /><br />" ... Shute has the faculty for seizing upon contemporary drama and weaving it into a story with very human elements. This is the story of a conservative, tradition-bound old Englishman, faced with the need to be needed, meeting it with quiet courage and no bombast. He is caught by rumors of German invasion, while on holiday in the Jura mountains, and is asked to take two English children to safety in England. In their checkered progress across invaded France, he takes under his wing other children, -- the niece of a matron at the Inn, a French child whose parents were killed by a dive bomber before his eyes, a Dutch urchin, and finally -- as the price of his own freedom, a German child, whose Jewish blood condemns her to perpetual escape. What a picture of refugee glutted roads, of German dive bombers, of terror -- and yet of the sentimental weak spot that exposes even the most hardened to the appeal of sheer goodness."</span>

  <span id="freeText16155562347910680671" style="display:none">A beautiful, heartwarming and encapsulating story about an elderly English man holidaying in France during World War II and coping with feelings of uselessness' and getting over the death in combat of his son,<br />While he is in France, that country is invaded by the Germans and two small English children come into his custody and he takes them under his wing with the aim of getting them to Britain.<br />He takes on the role of nurturer and protector and we get a window into France during the war and the German,an occupation.<br />Soon he comes across two French children, a lost Dutch urchin, a Jewish boy whose father was taken to his death in Auschwitz, and was hidden by a French farmer and eventually the small niece of a Nazi officer, whose mother it is said was not fully Aryan (likely part Jewish).<br />As well as being touching, the twists and turns are engaging and the focus on ordinary people in wartime is refreshing and timeless.</span>

<div id="review_246578528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/246578528" />
    <a title="Elizabeth (Alaska)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska"><img alt="Elizabeth (Alaska)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304966095p2/2026178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246578528?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth (Alaska)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth (Alaska)" href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska">Elizabeth (Alaska)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42934195-pied-piper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=mid-20th-century">mid-20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246578528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17645735883130374514">The premise is a simple one. Early in the second world war, a 70-year old man goes to an area of France near the border with Switzerland to do some fishing. He has visited this part of the country before. Although he served in the first world war, for reasons unknown to the reader, he doesn't seem to give much thought to the fact that another war has started. And why not? We know his son, a pilot, was killed in action. A flaw, but there would be no story had the author not placed him there.<br/><br/>Other</span>
  <span id="freeText17645735883130374514" style="display:none">The premise is a simple one. Early in the second world war, a 70-year old man goes to an area of France near the border with Switzerland to do some fishing. He has visited this part of the country before. Although he served in the first world war, for reasons unknown to the reader, he doesn't seem to give much thought to the fact that another war has started. And why not? We know his son, a pilot, was killed in action. A flaw, but there would be no story had the author not placed him there.<br /><br />Others in the area think there is more danger and he is entrusted to accompany two English children back to England. Before departing, a third child, French, but whose father is working in London, is added to the group. Although the trip is dangerous and doesn't go at all the way Mr. Howard has planned it, we know from the first pages that he returns successfully. The book opens with his having a brandy in his club with another fellow. They sit and, during a night of bombing, Mr. Howard tells his story.<br /><br />The characterization of Mr. Howard is good enough to have him believable, although it would be a stretch to say he is fully-fleshed. I'm not sure I fully bought into the other characterizations, but I'm hard put say exactly why. I was annoyed from the beginning about the writing style. For my tastes, it was too simple. I prefer more a complex sentence structure and vocabulary. After about the halfway point I stopped noticing. This is because this is really a plot-driven novel. While the ending is predictable, it is still an excellent story and I simply got caught up in it.<br /><br />I did expect more and perhaps it is my expectations that were too high rather than the novel being just OK. It was right for me at this time to have something not too sad or thought provoking. Still and all, it's just a solid 3-stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17645735883130374514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_260790129" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260790129" />
    <a title="Judy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7409820-judy"><img alt="Judy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548545778p2/7409820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/260790129?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judy" href="/user/show/7409820-judy">Judy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer260790129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17640185836954424997">Nevil Shute is such a wonderful storyteller. I wish we had more books by him. My library doesn't have many ; so I've been buying used copies of several of his books. It's my one concession to adding to my own library. I wonder if many younger readers even know of Shute. Even the several of his books that have been made into movies are quite old. This book is another of his WWII stories--an interesting tale of how an "old" man tried to help several children out of France as the Germans were invad</span>
  <span id="freeText17640185836954424997" style="display:none">Nevil Shute is such a wonderful storyteller. I wish we had more books by him. My library doesn't have many ; so I've been buying used copies of several of his books. It's my one concession to adding to my own library. I wonder if many younger readers even know of Shute. Even the several of his books that have been made into movies are quite old. This book is another of his WWII stories--an interesting tale of how an "old" man tried to help several children out of France as the Germans were invading. I was a bit amused by the fact that I am a number of years older than John Howard, the main protagonist. There are some "Britishisms" that an American has to figure out, and these are somewhat intensified by the passage of time. Still this is an exciting and heart-warming book. Now if someone would re-release <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107301.A_Town_Like_Alice" title="A Town Like Alice by Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener">A Town Like Alice</a> on film, I'd be happy. Of course the book is better, but Alice and Pied Piper are my favorites by Shute. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17640185836954424997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10303508574306177301"><strong>Thoroughly British, thoroughly enjoyable!</strong><br/><br/>Nevil Shute is the author of one of my favorite novels A Town Like Alice. I had not realized he had written quite a few more novels. This one, Pied Piper came highly recommended and rightfully so. It is a wonderful story, simple and deep. Thoroughly British</span>

<div id="review_1163803370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1163803370" />
    <a title="Carol Bakker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2534237-carol-bakker"><img alt="Carol Bakker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337830449p2/2534237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1163803370?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol Bakker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol Bakker" href="/user/show/2534237-carol-bakker">Carol Bakker</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2534237-carol-bakker?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2534237-carol-bakker?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2534237-carol-bakker?shelf=ww2">ww2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2534237-carol-bakker?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2534237-carol-bakker?shelf=europe">europe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2534237-carol-bakker?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2534237-carol-bakker?shelf=cozy">cozy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2534237-carol-bakker?shelf=elderly">elderly</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1163803370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1194279122435249875">John Howard's world has collapsed; the seventy-ish English man responds by going fishing in the Jura mountains in France. [friends of ours named their dog "Jura" after these mountains] When the Nazi army is poised to invade France, Howard betakes himself back to England. His trip back is complicated by two English children with whom he agreed to travel. They are hoping to get to St. Malo [a city I never heard of until two weeks ago when I read All the Light We Cannot See...and voila! it reappear</span>
  <span id="freeText1194279122435249875" style="display:none">John Howard's world has collapsed; the seventy-ish English man responds by going fishing in the Jura mountains in France. [friends of ours named their dog "Jura" after these mountains] When the Nazi army is poised to invade France, Howard betakes himself back to England. His trip back is complicated by two English children with whom he agreed to travel. They are hoping to get to St. Malo [a city I never heard of until two weeks ago when I read All the Light We Cannot See...and voila! it reappears in my reading!!] and take a boat across the channel.<br /><br />This is a cozy read, with a sentimental flavor that isn't off-putting. What made me love the book was John Howard's patience: patience with the slow pace, the children's limitations, the irritating circumstances, the incessant difficulties. He must have memorized the serenity prayer.<br /><br />When motion sickness causes a child to vomit: "For a moment he was startled and disgusted. Then patience came back to him; children couldn't help that sort of thing. She was coughing and weeping; he pulled out his handkerchief and wiped her face and comforted her."<br /><br />Another exchange I loved. "He felt himself in peril. This woman was quite capable of giving them all up to the Germans. He faced her boldly, and looked into her eyes, "Do you believe that England has abandoned France?" he asked. "Or do you think that is a German lie?" She hesitated. "These filthy politics," she said at last. "I only know that this farm now is ruined. I do not know how we shall live." He said simply, "By the Grace of God, madame." <br /><br />One last quote: "We spoke quietly as we lay relaxed beside each other in our chairs, with long pauses between sentences. When you are tired there is pleasure in a conversation taken in sips, like old brandy." <br /><br />I was surprised that this book was published in 1941, a short time after the Battle of Dunkirk, mentioned in this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1194279122435249875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer979304970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13396112570001754941">I really loved this story and the character of Mr. Howard, as the children called him. I loved his relationship he had with the children. As with most war stories, you see the bad, evil and ugly things that happen during this time. But in this story, you see something evolving that makes you feel good. I'm not sure if this was based on a true story or not but I wish it was. Mr. Howard you are a war Hero of a different kind!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4416150777982433535">I did enjoy this as a feel-good story. Mr Howard, the main character , trying to get himself and what started as two children, back to England from France towards the end of the war, picks up several other children en route. Mr Howard is a seventy year old English gentleman, and I only hope when I get to that age, I have his patience and strength.   <span id="freeText4416150777982433535" style="display:none">I did enjoy this as a feel-good story. Mr Howard, the main character , trying to get himself and what started as two children, back to England from France towards the end of the war, picks up several other children en route. Mr Howard is a seventy year old English gentleman, and I only hope when I get to that age, I have his patience and strength. The children acted as children will, but some of the help that Mr Howard got, did seem a bit far-fetched at times. The history of the setting was quite accurate, and made for a plausible story. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1883816-barbara-h?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2899675149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9509011124376705906">I had previously read books by Nevil Shute, namely ,<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38180.On_the_Beach' title='On the Beach by Nevil Shute' rel='nofollow noopener'>On the Beach</a> ,(1957); <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107301.A_Town_Like_Alice' title='A Town Like Alice by Nevil Shute' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Town Like Alice</a> ,(1950) ; both adapted to films. I was quite impressed and remembered them well. Clearly he was not a modern author, but I feel that most of his writing stands up well to time.<br/><br/>This book involves an elderly English gentleman who was on an extended vacation in France during 1940 when the Nazis invaded the country. While preparing to return to England, he agreed to transport two small children along for the </span>
  <span id="freeText9509011124376705906" style="display:none">I had previously read books by Nevil Shute, namely ,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38180.On_the_Beach" title="On the Beach by Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Beach</a> ,(1957); <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107301.A_Town_Like_Alice" title="A Town Like Alice by Nevil Shute" rel="nofollow noopener">A Town Like Alice</a> ,(1950) ; both adapted to films. I was quite impressed and remembered them well. Clearly he was not a modern author, but I feel that most of his writing stands up well to time.<br /><br />This book involves an elderly English gentleman who was on an extended vacation in France during 1940 when the Nazis invaded the country. While preparing to return to England, he agreed to transport two small children along for the trip. As the title implies, due to unforseen events, this carefully planned trek involved collecting more children along the way. As one could surmise during those perilous times, they encountered many unexpected incidents. Some of this involved a minor suspension of belief, but the narrative generally contained a reliable and enjoyable tension for the reader.<br /><br />Today I went to the library with hopes that now I had revived my association with this author and enjoyed this book so thoroughly, I could seek another of his novels. I was astounded! There was one long shelf devoted solely to his books, starting in the 1920's. Many were yellowed and some tattered without descriptions. I shall return at a later date with appropriately researched titles and information to find the one(s) I want to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9509011124376705906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1900713190" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1900713190" />
    <a title="Andy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2199404-andy"><img alt="Andy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331458678p2/2199404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1900713190?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy" href="/user/show/2199404-andy">Andy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/29956583-pied-piper">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1900713190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16162512802914590860">The timeliness of this book is astonishing. The historical story of refugees fleeing from the Nazi invasion of France is so compelling that it is still the subject of current bestsellers (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21853621.The_Nightingale' title='The Nightingale by Kristin Hannah' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Nightingale</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18143977.All_the_Light_We_Cannot_See' title='All the Light We Cannot See by Anthony Doerr' rel='nofollow noopener'>All the Light We Cannot See</a>). This is perhaps the first English language novel about the episode, so it's interesting from that standpoint, but also in the context of the refugee crisis in the news. <br/><br/>The plot is bizarre enough to be a page-turner, yet the initial premise is plausible, and the re</span>
  <span id="freeText16162512802914590860" style="display:none">The timeliness of this book is astonishing. The historical story of refugees fleeing from the Nazi invasion of France is so compelling that it is still the subject of current bestsellers (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21853621.The_Nightingale" title="The Nightingale by Kristin Hannah" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nightingale</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18143977.All_the_Light_We_Cannot_See" title="All the Light We Cannot See by Anthony Doerr" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Light We Cannot See</a>). This is perhaps the first English language novel about the episode, so it's interesting from that standpoint, but also in the context of the refugee crisis in the news. <br /><br />The plot is bizarre enough to be a page-turner, yet the initial premise is plausible, and the rest of the story holds together from there. While a brutally honest war story, it is also very human and touching. This is masterful storytelling.<br /><br /><b>Nerdy musings:</b> The writing at first felt sloppy, as if the author were rushing it out, but the more I read, the more I thought he was being deliberate. The word "presently" is used so frequently, that it's like a code word he's trying to get the reader to notice. As in, we need to react to this NOW. There are other bizarre usages too. "Desolated" is used to mean "I'm sorry" a lot. This would be a bad word-for-word translation from French of "désolé" but the author isn't French, the character isn't French and isn't necessarily even speaking French in the story when this word is used. So again, it seems like a sort of code for communicating how desperately serious the danger is. Who is Shute trying to get this across to? Americans I would guess, presumably pre-Pearl Harbor. Over and over again it is explained how kind-hearted the Americans are, and how they would want to help refugee children. Anyway, it would be interesting to find out if my interpretation is correct. Are there are some Shute experts out there?</span>
  <a data-text-id="16162512802914590860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_91338416" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91338416" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3230620-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1265303752p2/3230620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91338416?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/3230620-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099530220" href="/book/show/6084757-pied-piper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3230620-tim?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91338416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17712694047630147507">Recovering from the death of his Son, an RAF pilot during the early days of the War, elderly John Howard takes a Holiday in France close to the Swiss Border. The news of the War is sombre, the French Invasion by Germany is gathering pace, and is swooping southwards beyond Paris.<br/><br/>He is asked by friends to escort their two young children, back to England and embarks on a race against time to reach the atlantic coast and a passage to safety, before the advanzing Nazi forces consume France. Along the</span>
  <span id="freeText17712694047630147507" style="display:none">Recovering from the death of his Son, an RAF pilot during the early days of the War, elderly John Howard takes a Holiday in France close to the Swiss Border. The news of the War is sombre, the French Invasion by Germany is gathering pace, and is swooping southwards beyond Paris.<br /><br />He is asked by friends to escort their two young children, back to England and embarks on a race against time to reach the atlantic coast and a passage to safety, before the advanzing Nazi forces consume France. Along the journey he picks up other young Children that for a variety of reasons need to escape the War in France.<br /><br />Nevil Shute's Novel written in 1941 is equally exciting and uplifting. He paints a wonderful picture of reural/peasant France as they await the arrival of the "sale bosche". The tension builds as they enter occupied France and enlist the help of various Partisans and past acquaintances of his and of his Son,including his Sons French lover Nicole. <br /><br />John Howard is a typical "stiff upper lip" Englishmen, a perfect Gent in everyway, right down to his Harris Tweed attire and fly fishing pasttime. He is also portrayed by Shute as a vulnerable old man, but one with boundless humanity and a desire to do right by everyone he encounters.<br /><br />The writing is somewhat dated, but has unlimited charm and has you confiring with the dictionary (and "babelfish") regularly to understand the meaning of words now somewhat lost in the English Language, as well as the occasional use of french phrases. Rather than annoy, the use of french embelishes its quality and seems to add to the overall feel and authenticity of the Novel.<br /><br />As someone from the times might say, A rollicking, spiffing good yarn.<br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17712694047630147507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1203401771" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Hanna-col" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33963559-hanna-col"><img alt="Hanna-col" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586472186p2/33963559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hanna-col" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hanna-col" href="/user/show/33963559-hanna-col">Hanna-col</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780307474018" href="/book/show/7757032-pied-piper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33963559-hanna-col?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33963559-hanna-col?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1203401771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3921419390574763574"> I stumbled upon Pied Piper while going through a list of Nevil Shute’s works. The synopsis of the book piqued my interest and I almost bought it soon after while making an Amazon purchase (I opted out to buy Steal Like An Artist instead). Several weeks back, I received Pied Piper as a birthday gift from my parents and started reading it a few days later.<br/><br/> In the most simple of terms, I loved it. The idea of an old man trying to return to England as the Nazis invade France and taking refugee chil</span>
  <span id="freeText3921419390574763574" style="display:none"> I stumbled upon Pied Piper while going through a list of Nevil Shute’s works. The synopsis of the book piqued my interest and I almost bought it soon after while making an Amazon purchase (I opted out to buy Steal Like An Artist instead). Several weeks back, I received Pied Piper as a birthday gift from my parents and started reading it a few days later.<br /><br /> In the most simple of terms, I loved it. The idea of an old man trying to return to England as the Nazis invade France and taking refugee children with him appeals to my imagination and Nevil Shute did not disappointment. Pied Piper was everything I wanted it to be and then some.<br /><br /> As with the majority of my favorite books it was the characters that captured my heart most. John Sidney Howard might be an unlikely hero at the ripe old age of seventy but he is a compelling one. Feeling useless in England during the stalemate of the winter of 1939, he journeys to Southeast France in the spring of 1940 determined to fish and enjoy himself, unaware of the Nazi invasion of France about overtake him. When his perilous position finally does rouse him into returning to England, he is entrusted to take two English children to their aunt in England as well. Their journey is difficult from the outset but Mr. Howard is completely unprepared for just how arduous and difficult it becomes. As they straggle towards the coast, he finds himself taking more children under his wing even though he hardly knows what he will do with them.<br /><br /> Fans of historical fiction and WWII history buffs will find Pied Piper a treat, though be on the look out for occasional smatterings of language throughout. The bulk of foul language comes from the mouths of two RAF men Howard and the children travel with briefly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3921419390574763574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/409175840?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sally906" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sally906" href="/user/show/4949011-sally906">Sally906</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4949011-sally906?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4949011-sally906?shelf=australian-author">australian-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer409175840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17189021495024885799">The original Pied Piper of Hamelin story is a German Folk tale where a man offers to rid Hamelin of its rat problem for a fee – accepted he plays his pipes and the mice all follow him to be drowned in a river. However when the city leaders renege on the payment the piper plays another tune and the children all follow him into a gap in the mountain where it closes behind them and they are never seen again. I am not sure of the connection as Mr Howard is rescuing the children in this story rather </span>
  <span id="freeText17189021495024885799" style="display:none">The original Pied Piper of Hamelin story is a German Folk tale where a man offers to rid Hamelin of its rat problem for a fee – accepted he plays his pipes and the mice all follow him to be drowned in a river. However when the city leaders renege on the payment the piper plays another tune and the children all follow him into a gap in the mountain where it closes behind them and they are never seen again. I am not sure of the connection as Mr Howard is rescuing the children in this story rather than taking them to be vengeful. Still an elderly man leading children to freedom against a foe that means them harm is an uplifting theme. Nevil Shute wrote this book in 1942 – when WWII was still raging – and is set in 1940 when Germany invaded and occupied France; a dark time for the people of France. Shute is a master of building the tension without the in your face wham bam that many writers do today, you really don’t realise you’re on the edge of your seat until you have to put the book down and realise you can’t! There is violence in the book – but it is war after all – again the violence does not degenerate into pages of gore – but the fear and the senselessness of it all is all to evident. A very good read indeed.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17189021495024885799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115443588" />
    <a title="Phair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2613975-phair"><img alt="Phair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253154922p2/2613975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115443588?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phair" href="/user/show/2613975-phair">Phair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780307474018" href="/book/show/7757032-pied-piper">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115443588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11681149904524149749"> While this was published in 1941 and was about events of the 1940 German invasion of France, to me it was historical fiction made more interesting and real because of the immediacy. A very leisurely book about frantic events- the pace fit a story of a 70 year old man traveling, largely on foot, with a group of very young children. Seeing events through the eyes of the children who did not see the Germans as enemies but treated all people they met as befitted their actions- kind or friendly peop</span>
  <span id="freeText11681149904524149749" style="display:none"> While this was published in 1941 and was about events of the 1940 German invasion of France, to me it was historical fiction made more interesting and real because of the immediacy. A very leisurely book about frantic events- the pace fit a story of a 70 year old man traveling, largely on foot, with a group of very young children. Seeing events through the eyes of the children who did not see the Germans as enemies but treated all people they met as befitted their actions- kind or friendly people were friends, mean people were not, be they German or French. I liked that the book was written as a retelling of the story by a narrator who had it from the old man while they waited out a blitz attack in London at a gentleman's club. Knowing that the old man had survived to tell the tale lessened some of the tragic potential and allowed me to read with at least some hope for a happy ending. There was a little disbelief at the incredibly lucky happenstance that brought about the conclusion- it brought to mind Tarentino's Inglourious Basterds. This would make a good TV movie for sure. (3.5 stars)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11681149904524149749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14577983003166530584" style="display:none">The story teller relates how he meets, Sidney Howard, an old man at his club during the London Blitz. They settle down for a night of bombing with a glass of Marsala (probably more than one) and the old man relates the story of (spoiler alert!) how he had managed to get out of France where he’d gone on a fishing trip as the Germans were invading.
